      "text": "I\n119th CONGRESS\n1st Session\nH. R. 471\nIN THE HOUSE OF REPRESENTATIVES\nJanuary 16, 2025 Mr. Westerman (for himself, Mr. Peters , Mr. Tiffany , Mr. Panetta , Mr. Stauber , Mr. Whitesides , Mr. Collins , Mr. Vasquez , Mrs. Kim , Mr. Costa , Mr. Zinke , Mr. Harder of California , Mr. Johnson of South Dakota , Mr. Bera , Mrs. Kiggans of Virginia , Mr. Garamendi , Ms. Maloy , Mr. Thompson of California , Mr. Begich , Mr. Correa , Mr. Crank , Mr. Golden of Maine , Mr. Ezell , Mr. Mullin , Mr. Hurd of Colorado , Ms. Lee of Nevada , Mr. Valadao , Mr. Gray , Mr. Barr , Mr. Hoyer , Mr. Carter of Georgia , Ms. Pettersen , Mr. Joyce of Pennsylvania , Mr. Obernolte , Mr. Walberg , Mr. LaMalfa , Mr. Gosar , Ms. Boebert , Mr. McClintock , Mr. Issa , Mr. Fong , Ms. Hageman , Mr. Fry , and Mr. Amodei of Nevada ) introduced the following bill; which was referred to the Committee on Natural Resources , and in addition to the Committees on Agriculture , and Science, Space, and Technology , for a period to be subsequently determined by the Speaker, in each case for consideration of such provisions as fall within the jurisdiction of the committee concerned\nA BILL\nTo expedite under the National Environmental Policy Act of 1969 and improve forest management activities on National Forest System lands, on public lands under the jurisdiction of the Bureau of Land Management, and on Tribal lands to return resilience to overgrown, fire-prone forested lands, and for other purposes.\n#### 1. Short title; table of contents\n##### (a) Short title\nThis Act may be cited as the Fix Our Forests Act .\n##### (b) Table of contents\nThe table of contents for this Act is as follows:\nSec.\u20021.\u2002Short title; table of contents.\nSec.\u20022.\u2002Definitions.\nTitle I\u2014Landscape-Scale Restoration\nSubtitle A\u2014Addressing Emergency Wildfire Risks in High Priority Firesheds\nSec.\u2002101.\u2002Designation of fireshed management areas.\nSec.\u2002102.\u2002Fireshed center.\nSec.\u2002103.\u2002Fireshed registry.\nSec.\u2002104.\u2002Shared stewardship.\nSec.\u2002105.\u2002Fireshed assessments.\nSec.\u2002106.\u2002Emergency fireshed management.\nSec.\u2002107.\u2002Sunset.\nSubtitle B\u2014Expanding Collaborative Tools to Reduce Wildfire Risk and Improve Forest Health\nSec.\u2002111.\u2002Modification of the treatment of certain revenue and payments under good neighbor agreements.\nSec.\u2002112.\u2002Fixing stewardship end result contracting.\nSec.\u2002113.\u2002Intra-agency strike teams.\nSec.\u2002114.\u2002Locally-led restoration.\nSec.\u2002115.\u2002Joint Chiefs landscape restoration partnership program.\nSec.\u2002116.\u2002Collaborative forest landscape restoration program.\nSec.\u2002117.\u2002Utilizing grazing for wildfire risk reduction.\nSec.\u2002118.\u2002Water source protection program.\nSec.\u2002119.\u2002Watershed condition framework technical corrections.\nSubtitle C\u2014Litigation Reform\nSec.\u2002121.\u2002Commonsense litigation reform.\nSec.\u2002122.\u2002Consultation on forest plans.\nTitle II\u2014Protecting Communities in the Wildland-Urban Interface\nSec.\u2002201.\u2002Community wildfire risk reduction program.\nSec.\u2002202.\u2002Community wildfire defense research program.\nSec.\u2002203.\u2002Vegetation management, facility inspection, and operation and maintenance relating to electric transmission and distribution facility rights-of-way.\nSec.\u2002204.\u2002Categorical exclusion for electric utility lines rights-of-way.\nSec.\u2002205.\u2002Seeds of success.\nSec.\u2002206.\u2002Program to support priority reforestation and restoration projects of Department of the Interior.\nSec.\u2002207.\u2002Fire department repayment.\nTitle III\u2014Transparency, Technology, and Partnerships\nSubtitle A\u2014Transparency and Technology\nSec.\u2002301.\u2002Biochar innovations and opportunities for conservation, health, and advancements in research.\nSec.\u2002302.\u2002Accurate hazardous fuels reduction reports.\nSec.\u2002303.\u2002Public-private wildfire technology deployment and demonstration partnership.\nSec.\u2002304.\u2002GAO study on Forest Service policies.\nSec.\u2002305.\u2002Forest Service Western headquarters study.\nSec.\u2002306.\u2002Keeping forest plans current and monitored.\nSec.\u2002307.\u2002Container Aerial Firefighting System (CAFFS).\nSec.\u2002308.\u2002Study on pine beetle infestation.\nSubtitle B\u2014White Oak Resilience\nSec.\u2002311.\u2002White Oak Restoration Initiative Coalition.\nSec.\u2002312.\u2002Forest Service pilot program.\nSec.\u2002313.\u2002Department of the Interior white oak review and restoration.\nSec.\u2002314.\u2002White oak regeneration and upland oak habitat.\nSec.\u2002315.\u2002Tree nursery shortages.\nSec.\u2002316.\u2002White oak research.\nSec.\u2002317.\u2002USDA formal initiative.\nSec.\u2002318.\u2002Authorities.\nTitle IV\u2014Ensuring Casualty Assistance for our Firefighters\nSec.\u2002401.\u2002Wildland Fire Management Casualty Assistance Program.\n#### 2. Definitions\nIn this Act:\n**(1) Director**\nThe term Director means the Director of the Fireshed Center appointed under section 102.\n**(2) Fireshed**\nThe term fireshed means a landscape-scale area that faces similar wildfire threat where a response strategy could influence the wildfire outcome.\n**(3) Fireshed management project**\nThe term fireshed management project means a project under section 106.\n**(4) Fireshed Registry**\nThe term Fireshed Registry means the fireshed registry established under section 103.\n**(5) Forest plan**\nThe term forest plan means\u2014\n**(A)**\na land use plan prepared by the Bureau of Land Management for public lands pursuant to section 202 of the Federal Land Policy and Management Act of 1976 ( 43 U.S.C. 1712 );\n**(B)**\na land and resource management plan prepared by the Forest Service for a unit of the National Forest System pursuant to section 6 of the Forest and Rangeland Renewable Resources Planning Act of 1974 ( 16 U.S.C. 1604 ); or\n**(C)**\na forest management plan (as defined in section 304 of the National Indian Forests Resources Management Act ( 25 U.S.C. 3104 )) with respect to Indian forest land or rangeland.\n**(6) Governor**\nThe term Governor means the Governor or any other appropriate executive official of an affected State or Indian Tribe or the Commonwealth of Puerto Rico.\n**(7) Hazardous fuels management activities**\nThe term hazardous fuels management activities means any vegetation management activities (or combination thereof) that reduce the risk of wildfire, including mechanical thinning, mastication, prescribed burning, cultural burning (as determined by the applicable Indian Tribe), timber harvest, and grazing.\n**(8) HFRA terms**\nThe terms at-risk community , community wildfire protection plan , and wildland-urban interface have the meanings given such terms, respectively, in section 101 of the Healthy Forests Restoration Act of 2003 ( 16 U.S.C. 6511 ).\n**(9) Indian forest land or rangeland**\nThe term Indian forest land or rangeland means land that\u2014\n**(A)**\nis held in trust by, or with a restriction against alienation by, the United States for an Indian Tribe or a member of an Indian Tribe; and\n**(B)**\n**(i)**\n**(I)**\nis Indian forest land (as defined in section 304 of the National Indian Forest Resources Management Act ( 25 U.S.C. 3103 )); or\n**(II)**\nhas a cover of grasses, brush, or any similar vegetation; or\n**(ii)**\nformerly had a forest cover or vegetative cover that is capable of restoration.\n**(10) Indian Tribe**\nThe term Indian Tribe has the meaning given that term in section 4 of the Indian Self-Determination and Education Assistance Act ( 25 U.S.C. 5304 ).\n**(11) National Forest System lands**\nThe term National Forest System lands has the meaning given the term in section 11(a) of the Forest and Rangeland Renewable Resources Planning Act of 1974 ( 16 U.S.C. 1609 ).\n**(12) Public lands**\nThe term public lands has the meaning given that term in section 103 of the Federal Land Policy and Management Act of 1976 ( 43 U.S.C. 1702 ), except that the term includes Coos Bay Wagon Road Grant lands and Oregon and California Railroad Grant lands.\n**(13) Relevant Congressional Committees**\nThe term relevant Congressional Committees means\u2014\n**(A)**\nthe Committees on Natural Resources and Agriculture of the House of Representatives; and\n**(B)**\nthe Committees on Energy and Natural Resources and Agriculture, Nutrition, and Forestry of the Senate.\n**(14) Responsible official**\nThe term responsible official means an employee of the Department of the Interior or Forest Service who has the authority to make and implement a decision on a proposed action.\n**(15) Secretaries**\nThe term Secretaries means each of\u2014\n**(A)**\nthe Secretary of the Interior; and\n**(B)**\nthe Secretary of Agriculture.\n**(16) Secretary**\nThe term Secretary means the Secretary of Agriculture.\n**(17) Secretary concerned**\nThe term Secretary concerned means\u2014\n**(A)**\nthe Secretary of Agriculture, with respect to National Forest System lands; and\n**(B)**\nthe Secretary of the Interior, with respect to public lands.\n**(18) Special District**\nThe term special district means a political subdivision of a State that\u2014\n**(A)**\nhas significant budgetary autonomy or control;\n**(B)**\nwas created by or pursuant to the laws of the State for the purpose of performing a limited and specific governmental or proprietary function; and\n**(C)**\nis distinct from any other local government unit within the State.\n**(19) State**\nThe term State means each of the several States, the District of Columbia, and each territory of the United States.\nI\nLandscape-Scale Restoration\nA\nAddressing Emergency Wildfire Risks in High Priority Firesheds\n#### 101. Designation of fireshed management areas\n##### (a) Designation of fireshed management areas\n**(1) Initial designations**\nFor the period beginning on the date of enactment of this Act and ending on the date that is 5 years after the date of enactment of this Act, there are designated fireshed management areas, which\u2014\n**(A)**\nshall be comprised of individual landscape-scale firesheds identified as being a high risk fireshed in the Wildfire Crisis Strategy published by the Forest Service in January 2022;\n**(B)**\nshall be comprised of individual landscape-scale firesheds identified by the Secretary, in consultation with the Secretary of the Interior, as being in the top 20 percent of the 7,688 firesheds published by the Rocky Mountain Research Station of the Forest Service in 2019 for wildfire exposure based on the following criteria\u2014\n**(i)**\nwildfire exposure and corresponding risk to communities, including risk to life and structures;\n**(ii)**\nwildfire exposure and corresponding risk to municipal watersheds, including tribal water supplies and systems; and\n**(iii)**\nrisk of forest conversion due to wildfire;\n**(C)**\nshall not overlap with any other fireshed management areas;\n**(D)**\nmay contain Federal and non-Federal land, including Indian forest lands or rangelands; and\n**(E)**\nwhere the Secretary concerned shall carry out fireshed management projects.\n**(2) Further fireshed management area designations**\n**(A) In general**\nOn the date that is 5 years after the date of the enactment of this Act and every 5 years thereafter, the Secretary, in consultation with the Secretary of the Interior, shall submit to the relevant Congressional Committees an updated map of firesheds based on the Fireshed Registry maintained under section 103.\n**(B) Designation**\nNot later than 60 days after submitting an updated fireshed map under subparagraph (A), the Secretary shall, based on such map, designate additional fireshed management areas that are identified as being in the top 20 percent of firesheds at risk of wildfire exposure based on the criteria specified in subparagraphs (B), (C), (D), and (E) of paragraph (1).\n##### (b) Applicability of NEPA\nThe designation of fireshed management areas under this section shall not be subject to the requirements of the National Environmental Policy Act of 1969 ( 42 U.S.C. 4321 et seq. ).\n#### 102. Fireshed center\n##### (a) Establishment\n**(1) In general**\nThe Secretary, acting through the Chief of the Forest Service, and the Secretary of the Interior, acting through the Director of the U.S. Geological Survey, shall jointly establish an interagency center, to be known as the Fireshed Center (hereinafter referred to as the Center ) to carry out the purposes in subsection (b).\n**(2) Composition**\n**(A) Divisions**\nThe Center shall be comprised of the following divisions:\n**(i)**\nTechnology and Engineering.\n**(ii)**\nData Services.\n**(iii)**\nAnalysis and Prediction.\n**(iv)**\nEducation and Consultation.\n**(B) Representatives**\nThe Center shall be comprised of at least one career representative from each of the following:\n**(i)**\nThe Forest Service.\n**(ii)**\nThe Bureau of Land Management.\n**(iii)**\nThe National Park Service.\n**(iv)**\nThe Bureau of Indian Affairs.\n**(v)**\nThe U.S. Fish and Wildlife Service.\n**(vi)**\nThe U.S. Geological Survey.\n**(vii)**\nThe Department of Defense.\n**(viii)**\nThe Department of Homeland Security.\n**(ix)**\nThe Department of Energy.\n**(x)**\nThe Federal Emergency Management Agency.\n**(xi)**\nThe National Science Foundation.\n**(xii)**\nThe National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration.\n**(xiii)**\nThe National Aeronautics and Space Administration.\n**(xiv)**\nThe National Institute of Standards and Technology.\n**(xv)**\nThe United States Fire Administration.\n**(C) Appointments**\nEach representative of a Department, Agency, or other entity specified in subparagraph (B) shall be appointed by the head of that Department, Agency, or other entity, as applicable.\n**(3) Director**\nThe representatives appointed under paragraph (2) shall, by majority vote, appoint a Director of the Center, who\u2014\n**(A)**\nshall be an employee of the U.S. Geological Survey or the Forest Service;\n**(B)**\nshall serve an initial term of not more than 7 years;\n**(C)**\nmay serve one additional term of not more than 7 years after the initial term described in subparagraph (B); and\n**(D)**\nshall be responsible for the management and operation of the Center.\n**(4) Associate directors**\nIn consultation with the representatives appointed under paragraph (2), the Director may appoint such Associate Directors as the Director determines necessary.\n**(5) Additional representation**\nThe Secretary, acting through the Chief of the Forest Service, and the Secretary of the Interior, acting through the Director of the U.S. Geological Survey, may jointly appoint additional representatives of Federal agencies, States, Indian Tribes, or local governments to the Center, as the Secretaries determine necessary.\n##### (b) Purposes\nThe purposes of the Center are to\u2014\n**(1)**\ncomprehensively assess and predict, using data tools (including artificial intelligence) and other decision support products, fire and smoke in the wildland and built environment interface across jurisdictions to inform\u2014\n**(A)**\nland and fuels management;\n**(B)**\ncommunity (including at-risk communities identified in fireshed assessments conducted under section 105) and built environment risk reduction, including the support and development of community wildfire protection plans and evacuation decisions; and\n**(C)**\npublic health risk reduction related to wildland fire and smoke, including air quality monitoring and forecasting and smoke prediction models;\n**(D)**\nfire response and management, including the pre-positioning of wildfire suppression personnel and assets based on real-time risk; and\n**(E)**\npost-fire recovery activities, including activities related to vegetation recovery, debris flows and flooding, watershed recovery and protection, and ecosystem health;\n**(2)**\nprovide data aggregation, real-time land and fuels management services, and science-based decision support services to inform the purposes specified in subparagraph (A) through (E) of paragraph (1);\n**(3)**\nreduce fragmentation and duplication across Federal land management agencies with respect to predictive service and decision support functions related to wildland fire and smoke, including through the provision of data aggregation described in paragraph (2);\n**(4)**\npromote coordination and sharing of data regarding wildland fire and smoke decision making (including through the provision of data aggregation described in paragraph (2)) to each of the entities specified in subparagraphs (A) through (F) of paragraph (8);\n**(5)**\nstreamline procurement processes for technologies (including technologies identified under the pilot program established under section 303) and cybersecurity systems related to addressing wildland fire and smoke for the purposes of scaling such technologies and systems across Federal agencies;\n**(6)**\namplify and distribute existing, and develop as necessary, publicly accessible data, models, technologies (including mapping technologies), assessments, and National Weather Service fire weather forecasts to support short- and long-term planning regarding wildland fire and smoke risk reduction and post-fire recovery while avoiding duplicative efforts, as determined by the Director;\n**(7)**\nmaintain the Fireshed Registry established under section 103; and\n**(8)**\ndisseminate data tools (including artificial intelligence) and other decision support products, for use in manners consistent with the purposes described paragraphs (1) through (7), to the following:\n**(A)**\nFederal agencies.\n**(B)**\nIndian Tribes.\n**(C)**\nState and local governments.\n**(D)**\nAcademic or research institutions.\n**(E)**\nWildland firefighting entities, including applicable incident management teams and geographic coordination centers.\n**(F)**\nOther entities, including public, private, and nonprofit entities, with expertise in land management, air quality, water management, or public health, as determined appropriate by the Director.\n##### (c) Memoranda of understanding\nThe Center may enter into memoranda of understanding, contracts, or other agreements with State governments, Indian Tribes, local governments, academic or research institutions, and private entities to improve the information and operations of the Center.\n##### (d) Administrative support, technical services, and staff support\n**(1) USGS support**\nThe Secretary of the Interior shall make personnel of the U.S. Geological Survey available to the Center for such administrative support, technical services, and development and dissemination of data as the Secretary determines necessary to carry out this section.\n**(2) USFS support**\nThe Secretary shall make personnel of the Forest Service available to the Center for such administrative support, technical services, and the development and dissemination of information related to fireshed management and the Fireshed Registry as the Secretary determines necessary to carry out this section.\n**(3) Funding**\nNotwithstanding section 708 of title VII of division E of the Consolidated Appropriations Act, 2023 ( Public Law 117\u2013328 ), the Secretary of the Interior and Secretary may enter into agreements to share the management and operational costs of the Center.\n##### (e) Rule of construction\nNothing in this section shall be construed to affect the ownership of any data sources.\n#### 103. Fireshed registry\n##### (a) Fireshed registry\nThe Secretary, acting through the Director of the Fireshed Center appointed under section 102, shall maintain a Fireshed Registry on a publicly accessible website that provides interactive geospatial data on individual firesheds, including information on\u2014\n**(1)**\nwildfire exposure delineated by ownership, including rights-of-way for utilities and other public or private purposes;\n**(2)**\nany hazardous fuels management activities that have occurred within an individual fireshed in the past 10 years;\n**(3)**\nwildfire exposure with respect to such fireshed delineated by\u2014\n**(A)**\nwildfire exposure and corresponding risk to communities, including risk to life and structures;\n**(B)**\nwildfire exposure and corresponding risk to municipal watersheds, including tribal water supplies and systems; and\n**(C)**\nrisk of forest conversion due to wildfire;\n**(4)**\nthe percentage of the fireshed that has burned in wildfires in the past 10 years, including, to the extent practicable, delineations of acres that have burned at a high severity;\n**(5)**\nspatial patterns of wildfire exposure, including plausible extreme fire events; and\n**(6)**\nany hazardous fuels management activities planned for the fireshed, including fireshed management projects.\n##### (b) Community Wildfire Protection Plans\nThe Director shall make data from the Fireshed Registry available to local communities developing or updating community wildfire protection plans.\n##### (c) Requirement to maintain\nAs part of the website containing the Fireshed Registry, the Director shall\u2014\n**(1)**\npublish fireshed assessments created under section 105; and\n**(2)**\nmaintain a searchable database to track\u2014\n**(A)**\nthe status of Federal environmental reviews, permits, and authorizations for fireshed management projects, including\u2014\n**(i)**\na comprehensive permitting timetable;\n**(ii)**\nthe status of the compliance of each lead agency, cooperating agency, and participating agency with the permitting timetable with respect to such fireshed management projects;\n**(iii)**\nany modifications of the permitting timetable required under clause (i), including an explanation as to why the permitting timetable was modified; and\n**(iv)**\ninformation about project-related public meetings, public hearings, and public comment periods, which shall be presented in English and the predominant language of the community or communities most affected by the project, as that information becomes available;\n**(B)**\nthe projected cost of such fireshed management projects; and\n**(C)**\nin the case of completed fireshed management projects, the effectiveness of such projects in reducing the wildfire exposure within an applicable fireshed, including wildfire exposure described in subparagraphs (A) through (C) of subsection (a)(3).\n##### (d) Reliance on existing assessments\nIn carrying out this section, the Director may rely on assessments completed or data gather through existing partnerships, to the extent practicable.\n#### 104. Shared stewardship\n##### (a) Joint agreements\nNot later than 90 days after receiving a written request from a Governor of a State or an Indian Tribe, the Secretary concerned shall enter into a shared stewardship agreement (or similar agreement) with such Governor or Indian Tribe to jointly\u2014\n**(1)**\npromote the reduction of wildfire exposure, based on the criteria in section 101(a)(1)(B), in fireshed management areas across jurisdictional boundaries; and\n**(2)**\nconduct fireshed assessments under section 105.\n##### (b) Additional fireshed management areas\nWith respect to a shared stewardship agreement (or similar agreement) with a Governor of a State or an Indian Tribe entered into under subsection (a), the Secretary concerned, if requested by such Governor or Indian Tribe, may\u2014\n**(1)**\ndesignate additional fireshed management areas under such agreement; and\n**(2)**\nupdate such agreement to address new wildfire threats.\n#### 105. Fireshed assessments\n##### (a) Fireshed assessments\n**(1) In general**\nNot later than 90 days after the date on which the Secretary concerned enters into an agreement with a Governor of a State or an Indian Tribe under section 104, the Secretary concerned and such Governor or Indian Tribe shall, with respect to the fireshed management areas designated in such State, jointly conduct a fireshed assessment that\u2014\n**(A)**\nidentifies\u2014\n**(i)**\nusing the best available science, wildfire exposure risks within each such fireshed management area, including scenario planning and wildfire hazard mapping and models; and\n**(ii)**\neach at-risk community within each fireshed management area;\n**(B)**\nidentifies potential fireshed management projects to be carried out in such fireshed management areas, giving priority\u2014\n**(i)**\nprimarily, to projects with the purpose of reducing\u2014\n**(I)**\nwildfire exposure and corresponding risk to communities, including risk to life and structures;\n**(II)**\nwildfire exposure and corresponding risk to municipal watersheds, including tribal water supplies and systems;\n**(III)**\nrisk of forest conversion due to wildfire; or\n**(IV)**\nany combination of purposes described in subclauses (I) through (III); and\n**(ii)**\nsecondarily, to projects with the purpose of protecting\u2014\n**(I)**\ncritical infrastructure, including utility infrastructure;\n**(II)**\nwildlife habitats, including habitat for species listed under the Endangered Species Act ( 16 U.S.C. 1531 et seq. );\n**(III)**\nthe built environment, including residential and commercial buildings;\n**(IV)**\nresources of an Indian Tribe, as defined by the Indian Tribe; or\n**(V)**\nany combination of purposes described in subclauses (I) through (IV);\n**(C)**\nincludes\u2014\n**(i)**\na strategy for reducing the threat of wildfire to at-risk communities in the wildland-urban interface on both Federal and non-Federal land;\n**(ii)**\na timeline for the implementation of fireshed management projects;\n**(iii)**\nlong-term benchmark goals for the completion of fireshed management projects in the highest wildfire exposure areas so that such projects contribute to the development and maintenance of healthy and resilient landscapes;\n**(iv)**\npolicies to ensure fireshed management projects comply with applicable forest plans and incorporate the best available science; and\n**(v)**\na strategy for reducing the threat of wildfire to improve the effectiveness of wildland firefighting, particularly the effectiveness of fuels treatments that would improve wildland firefighter safety during wildfires;\n**(D)**\nshall be regularly updated based on the best available science, as determined by the Secretary concerned; and\n**(E)**\nshall be publicly available on a website maintained by the Secretary concerned.\n**(2) Local government participation**\nUpon the written request of a local government, the Secretary concerned and the Governor of the State in which the local government is located may allow such local government to participate in producing the fireshed assessment under paragraph (1) for such State.\n**(3) Information improvement**\n**(A) Memoranda of understanding**\nIn carrying out a fireshed assessment under this subsection, the Secretary concerned may enter into memoranda of understanding with other Federal agencies or departments (including the National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration), States, Indian Tribes, private entities, or research or educational institutions to improve, with respect to such assessment, the use and integration of\u2014\n**(i)**\nadvanced remote sensing and geospatial technologies;\n**(ii)**\nstatistical modeling and analysis; or\n**(iii)**\nany other technology or combination of technologies and analyses that the Secretary concerned determines will benefit the quality of information of such an assessment.\n**(B) Best available science**\nIn using the best available science for the fireshed assessments completed under subsection (a)(1), the Secretary concerned and Governor shall, to the maximum extent practicable, incorporate\u2014\n**(i)**\ntraditional ecological knowledge from Indian Tribes;\n**(ii)**\ndata from State forest action plans and State wildfire risk assessments;\n**(iii)**\ndata from the Fireshed Registry maintained under section 103; and\n**(iv)**\ndata from other Federal, State, Tribal, and local governments or agencies.\n##### (b) Applicability of NEPA\nFireshed assessments conducted under this section shall not be subject to the requirements of the National Environmental Policy Act of 1969 ( 42 U.S.C. 4321 et seq. ).\n#### 106. Emergency fireshed management\n##### (a) Fireshed management projects\n**(1) In general**\nThe Secretary concerned, acting through a responsible official, shall carry out fireshed management projects in fireshed management areas designated under section 101 in accordance with this section.\n**(2) Fireshed management projects**\nThe responsible official shall carry out the following forest and vegetation management activities as fireshed management projects under this section:\n**(A)**\nConducting hazardous fuels management activities.\n**(B)**\nCreating fuel breaks and fire breaks.\n**(C)**\nRemoving hazard trees, dead trees, dying trees, or trees at risk of dying, as determined by the responsible official.\n**(D)**\nDeveloping, approving, or conducting routine maintenance under a vegetation management, facility inspection, and operation and maintenance plan submitted under section 512(c)(1) of the Federal Land Policy and Management Act of 1976 ( 43 U.S.C. 1772(c)(1) ).\n**(E)**\nRemoving trees to address overstocking or crowding in a forest stand, consistent with the appropriate basal area of the forest stand as determined by the responsible official.\n**(F)**\nUsing chemical or re-seeding and planting treatments to address insects and disease and control vegetation competition or invasive species.\n**(G)**\nAny activities recommended by an applicable fireshed assessment carried out under section 105.\n**(H)**\nAny activities recommended by an applicable community wildfire protection plan.\n**(I)**\nAny combination of activities described in this paragraph.\n**(3) Emergency fireshed management**\n**(A) In general**\nFor any fireshed management area designated under section 101, the following shall have the force and effect of law:\n**(i)**\nSection 220.4(b) of title 36, Code of Federal Regulations (as in effect on the date of enactment of this Act), with respect to lands under the jurisdiction of the Secretary.\n**(ii)**\nSection 46.150 of title 43, Code of Federal Regulations (as in effect on the date of enactment of this Act), with respect to lands under the jurisdiction of the Secretary of the Interior.\n**(iii)**\nSection 402.05 of title 50, Code of Federal Regulations (as in effect on the date of enactment of this Act).\n**(iv)**\nSection 800.12 of title 36, Code of Federal Regulations (as in effect on the date of enactment of this Act).\n**(B) Utilization of existing streamlined authorities in fireshed management areas**\n**(i) In general**\nFireshed management projects carried out under this section shall be considered authorized projects under the following categorical exclusions:\n**(I)**\nSection 603(a) of the Healthy Forests Restoration Act of 2003 ( 16 U.S.C. 6591b(a) ).\n**(II)**\nSection 605(a) of the Healthy Forests Restoration Act of 2003 ( 16 U.S.C. 6591d(a) ).\n**(III)**\nSection 606(b) of the Healthy Forests Restoration Act of 2003 ( 16 U.S.C. 6591e(b) ).\n**(IV)**\nSection 40806(b) of the Infrastructure Investment and Jobs Act ( 16 U.S.C. 6592b(b) ).\n**(V)**\nSection 4(c)(4) of the Lake Tahoe Restoration Act ( Public Law 106\u2013506 ; 114 Stat. 2353).\n**(ii) Additional emergency actions**\nSubsection (d) of section 40807 of the Infrastructure Investment and Jobs Act ( 16 U.S.C. 6592c ) shall apply to fireshed management projects under this section in the same manner as such subsection applies to authorized emergency actions (as defined in subsection (a) of such section 40807) under such section 40807.\n**(iii) Use of expedited authorities**\nIn carrying out a fireshed management project, the Secretary shall apply a categorical exclusion under clause (i)\u2014\n**(I)**\nin a manner consistent with the statute establishing such categorical exclusion; and\n**(II)**\nin any area\u2014\n**(aa)**\ndesignated as suitable for timber production within the applicable forest plan; or\n**(bb)**\nwhere timber harvest activities are not prohibited.\n**(iv) Fiscal Responsibility Act requirements**\nIn carrying out this section, the Secretary concerned shall ensure compliance with the amendments made to the National Environmental Policy Act ( 42 U.S.C. 4321 et seq. ) by the Fiscal Responsibility Act of 2023 ( Public Law 118\u20135 ).\n**(v) Use of other authorities**\nTo the maximum extent practicable, the Secretary concerned shall use the authorities provided under this section in combination with other authorities to carry out fireshed management projects, including\u2014\n**(I)**\ngood neighbor agreements entered into under section 8206 of the Agricultural Act of 2014 ( 16 U.S.C. 2113a ) (as amended by this Act);\n**(II)**\nstewardship contracting projects entered into under section 604 of the Healthy Forests Restoration Act of 2003 ( 16 U.S.C. 6591c ) (as amended by this Act);\n**(III)**\nself-determination contracts and self-governance compact agreements entered into under the Indian Self-Determination and Education Assistance Act ( 25 U.S.C. 5301 et seq. ); and\n**(IV)**\nagreements entered into under the Tribal Forest Protection Act of 2004 ( 25 U.S.C. 3115a et seq. ).\n##### (b) Expansion\n**(1) HFRA amendments**\nThe Healthy Forests Restoration Act of 2003 is amended\u2014\n**(A)**\nin section 3 ( 16 U.S.C. 6502 ), by inserting at the end the following:\n(3) Local Government The term local government means a county, municipality, or special district. (4) Special District The term special district means a political subdivision of a State that\u2014 (A) has significant budgetary autonomy or control; (B) was created by or pursuant to the laws of the State for the purpose of performing a limited and specific governmental or proprietary function; and (C) is distinct from any other local government unit within the State. .\n**(B)**\nin section 603(c)(1) ( 16 U.S.C. 6591b(c)(1) ), by striking 3000 acres and inserting 10,000 acres ;\n**(C)**\nin section 603(c)(2)(B) ( 16 U.S.C. 6591b(c)(2)(B) ), by striking Fire Regime Groups I, II, or III and inserting Fire Regime I, Fire Regime II, Fire Regime III, Fire Regime IV, or Fire Regime V ;\n**(D)**\nin section 605(c)(1) ( 16 U.S.C. 6591d(c)(1) ), by striking 3000 acres and inserting 10,000 acres ; and\n**(E)**\nin section 606(g) ( 16 U.S.C. 6591e(g) ), by striking 4,500 acres and inserting 10,000 acres .\n**(2) Infrastructure Investment and Jobs Act amendment**\nSection 40806(d)(1) of the Infrastructure Investment and Jobs Act ( 16 U.S.C. 6592b(d)(1) ), by striking 3,000 acres and inserting 10,000 acres .\n**(3) Lake Tahoe Restoration Act amendments**\nSection 4(c)(4)(C) of the Lake Tahoe Restoration Act ( Public Law 106\u2013506 ; 114 Stat. 2353) is amended\u2014\n**(A)**\nby striking Lake Tahoe Basin Management Unit ; and\n**(B)**\nby inserting applicable to the area before the period at the end.\n#### 107. Sunset\nThe authority under this subtitle shall terminate on the date that is 7 years after the date of enactment of this Act.\nB\nExpanding Collaborative Tools to Reduce Wildfire Risk and Improve Forest Health\n#### 111. Modification of the treatment of certain revenue and payments under good neighbor agreements\n##### (a) Good neighbor authority\nSection 8206 of the Agricultural Act of 2014 ( 16 U.S.C. 2113a ) is amended\u2014\n**(1)**\nin subsection (a)(6), by striking or Indian tribe ;\n**(2)**\nin subsection (a), by inserting the following:\n(11) Special District The term special district means a political subdivision of a State that\u2014 (A) has significant budgetary autonomy or control; (B) was created by or pursuant to the laws of the State for the purpose of performing a limited and specific governmental or proprietary function; and (C) is distinct from any other local government unit within the State. .\n**(3)**\nin subsection (b)\u2014\n**(A)**\nin paragraph (1)(A), by inserting , Indian Tribe, special district, after Governor ;\n**(B)**\nin paragraph (2)(C)\u2014\n**(i)**\nin clause (i)\u2014\n**(I)**\nby inserting special district, after Indian Tribe, each place it appears;\n**(II)**\nin subclause (I)\u2014\n**(aa)**\nby striking on ; and\n**(bb)**\nby striking ; and and inserting a semicolon;\n**(III)**\nin subclause (II)(bb), by striking the period at the end and inserting a semicolon; and\n**(IV)**\nby adding at the end the following:\n(III) to construct new permanent roads on Federal lands that are\u2014 (aa) necessary to implement authorized restoration activities; and (bb) approved by the Federal agency through an environmental analysis or categorical exclusion decision; (IV) to complete new permanent road construction to replace and decommission an existing permanent road that is adversely impacting forest, rangeland, or watershed health; and (V) if there are funds remaining after carrying out subclauses (I) through (IV), to carry out authorized restoration services under other good neighbor agreements and for the administration of a good neighbor authority program by a Governor, Indian tribe, special district, or county. ; and\n**(ii)**\nin clause (ii), by striking 2028 and inserting 2030 ; and\n**(C)**\nin paragraph (3), by inserting , Indian Tribe, special district, after Governor ; and\n**(D)**\nby striking paragraph (4).\n##### (b) Conforming amendments\nSection 8206(a) of the Agricultural Act of 2014 ( 16 U.S.C. 2113a(a) ) is amended\u2014\n**(1)**\nin paragraph (1)(B), by inserting , Indian Tribe, special district, after Governor ; and\n**(2)**\nin paragraph (5), by inserting , Indian Tribe, special district, after Governor .\n##### (c) Effective date\nThe amendments made by this section apply to any project initiated pursuant to a good neighbor agreement (as defined in section 8206(a) of the Agricultural Act of 2014 ( 16 U.S.C. 2113a(a) ))\u2014\n**(1)**\nbefore the date of enactment of this Act, if the project was initiated after the date of enactment of the Agriculture Improvement Act of 2018 ( Public Law 115\u2013334 ; 132 Stat. 4490); or\n**(2)**\non or after the date of enactment of this Act.\n#### 112. Fixing stewardship end result contracting\nSection 604 of the Healthy Forests Restoration Act of 2003 ( 16 U.S.C. 6591c ) is amended\u2014\n**(1)**\nin subsection (b), by inserting , including retaining and expanding existing forest products infrastructure before the period at the end;\n**(2)**\nin subsection (d)(3)(B), by striking 10 years and inserting 20 years ; and\n**(3)**\nin subsection (h), by adding at the end the following:\n(4) Special rule for long-term stewardship contracts (A) In general A long-term agreement or contract entered into with an entity under subsection (b) by the Chief or the Director shall provide that in the case of the cancellation or termination by the Chief or the Director of such long-term agreement or contract, the Chief or the Director, as applicable, shall provide 10 percent of the agreement or contract amount to such entity as cancellation or termination costs. (B) Definition of long-term agreement or contract In this paragraph, the term long-term agreement or contract means an agreement or contract under subsection (b)\u2014 (i) with a term of more than 5 years; and (ii) entered into on or after the date of the enactment of this paragraph. .\n#### 113. Intra-agency strike teams\n##### (a) Establishment\nThe Secretary concerned shall establish intra-agency strike teams to assist the Secretary concerned with\u2014\n**(1)**\nany reviews, including analysis under the National Environmental Policy Act of 1969 ( 42 U.S.C. 4321 et seq. ), consultations under the National Historic Preservation Act of 1966 ( 16 U.S.C. 470 et seq. ), and consultations under the Endangered Species Act of 1973 ( 16 U.S.C. 1531 et seq. ), with the intent to accelerate and streamline interagency consultation processes;\n**(2)**\nthe implementation of any necessary site preparation work in advance of or as part of a fireshed management project;\n**(3)**\nthe implementation of fireshed management projects under such section; and\n**(4)**\nany combination of purposes under paragraphs (1) through (3).\n##### (b) Members\nThe Secretary concerned may appoint not more than 10 individuals to serve on an intra-agency strike team comprised of\u2014\n**(1)**\nemployees of the Department under the jurisdiction of the Secretary concerned;\n**(2)**\nemployees of a different Federal agency, with the consent of that agency\u2019s Secretary;\n**(3)**\nprivate contractors from any nonprofit organization, State government, Indian Tribe, local government, quasi-governmental agency, academic institution, or private organization; and\n**(4)**\nvolunteers from any nonprofit organization, State government, Indian Tribe, local government, quasi-governmental agency, academic institution, or private organization.\n##### (c) Sunset\nThe authority provided under this section shall terminate on the date that is 7 years after the date of enactment of this Act.\n#### 114. Utilizing grazing for wildfire risk reduction\nThe Secretary, acting through the Chief of the Forest Service, in coordination with holders of permits to graze livestock on Federal land, shall develop a strategy to increase opportunities to utilize livestock grazing as a wildfire risk reduction strategy, including\u2014\n**(1)**\ncompletion of reviews (as required under the National Environmental Policy Act of 1969 (U.S.C. 4321 et seq.)) to allow permitted grazing on vacant grazing allotments during instances of drought, wildfire, or other natural disasters that disrupt grazing on allotments already permitted;\n**(2)**\nuse of targeted grazing;\n**(3)**\nincreased use of temporary permits to promote targeted fuels reduction and reduction of invasive annual grasses;\n**(4)**\nincreased use of grazing as a postfire recovery and restoration strategy, where appropriate; and\n**(5)**\nuse of all applicable authorities under the law.\n#### 118. Water source protection program\nSection 303 of the Healthy Forests Restoration Act of 2003 ( 16 U.S.C. 6542(g)(4)(B) ) is amended\u2014\n**(1)**\nin subsection (a)\u2014\n**(A)**\nby redesignating paragraphs (1) through (7) as paragraphs (2) through (8), respectively;\n**(B)**\nby inserting before paragraph (2), as so redesignated, the following:\n(1) Adjacent land The term adjacent land means non-Federal land, including State, local, and private land, that is adjacent to, and within the same watershed as, National Forest System land on which a watershed protection and restoration project is carried out under this section. ; and\n**(C)**\nin paragraph (2), as so redesignated\u2014\n**(i)**\nby redesignating subparagraphs (G) and (H) as subparagraphs (K) and (L), respectively; and\n**(ii)**\nby inserting after subparagraph (F) the following:\n(G) an acequia association; (H) a local, regional, or other public entity that manages stormwater or wastewater resources or other related water infrastructure; (I) a land-grant mercedes; (J) a local, regional, or other private entity that has water delivery authority; ;\n**(2)**\nin subsection (b)\u2014\n**(A)**\nby striking The Secretary shall and inserting the following:\n(1) In general The Secretary shall ; and\n**(B)**\nby adding at the end the following:\n(2) Requirements A watershed protection and restoration project under the Program shall be designed to\u2014 (A) protect and restore watershed health, water supply and quality, a municipal or agricultural water supply system, and water-related infrastructure; (B) protect and restore forest health from insect infestation and disease or wildfire; or (C) advance any combination of the purposes described in subparagraphs (A) and (B). (3) Priorities In selecting watershed protection and restoration projects under the Program, the Secretary shall give priority to projects that would\u2014 (A) provide risk management benefits associated with: drought; wildfire; post-wildfire conditions; extreme weather; flooding; resilience to climate change; and watershed and fire resilience, including minimizing risks to watershed health, water supply and quality, and water-related infrastructure, including municipal and agricultural water supply systems; (B) support aquatic restoration and conservation efforts that complement existing or planned forest restoration or wildfire risk reduction efforts; or (C) provide quantifiable benefits to water supply or quality and include the use of nature-based solutions, such as restoring wetland and riparian ecosystems. (4) Conditions for projects on adjacent land (A) In general No project or activity may be carried out under this section on adjacent land unless the owner of the adjacent land agrees in writing that the owner is a willing and engaged partner in carrying out that project or activity. (B) Effect Nothing in this section shall be construed to authorize any change in\u2014 (i) the ownership of adjacent land on which a project or activity is carried out under this section; or (ii) the management of adjacent land on which a project or activity is carried out under this section, except during the carrying out of that project or activity. ;\n**(3)**\nin subsection (c)\u2014\n**(A)**\nin paragraph (1), by striking with end water users and inserting\nwith end water users to protect and restore the condition of National Forest watersheds and adjacent land that provide water\u2014 (A) to the end water users subject to the agreement; and\n**(iii)**\nby inserting after subparagraph (C) the following:\n(D) a good neighbor agreement entered into under section 8206 of the Agricultural Act of 2014 ( 16 U.S.C. 2113a ); or ; and\n**(C)**\nby adding at the end the following:\n(3) Cooperation with non-Federal partners The Secretary shall cooperate with non-Federal partners in carrying out assessments, planning, project design, and project implementation under this section. ;\n**(4)**\nin subsection (d)\u2014\n**(A)**\nby amending paragraph (2) to read as follows:\n(2) Requirement A water source management plan shall be\u2014 (A) designed to protect and restore ecological integrity (as defined in section 219.19 of title 36, Code of Federal Regulations (as in effect on the date of enactment of this subparagraph));
